## GHSA-pwx3-qcgw-vh7h · gogs.io/gogs

2026-06-23 · Go · **HIGH** 8.8 · Pattern: `CSRF→STATE_CHANGE`

### Root cause

The application was vulnerable to Cross-Site Request Forgery (CSRF) because it did not implement sufficient CSRF protection mechanisms for sensitive actions, specifically those related to changing an organization owner. An attacker could craft a malicious webpage that, when visited by an logged-in administrator, would trigger a request to change the organization owner without the administrator's explicit consent.

### Impact

An attacker could trick an organization owner into unknowingly transferring ownership of an organization to an attacker-controlled account, leading to a full takeover of the organization.

### Fix summary

The provided diff only shows changes to a minified CSS file, `gogs.min.css`. This CSS change alone does not address a CSRF vulnerability. A proper fix for CSRF would involve implementing CSRF tokens for state-changing operations, checking the `Referer` header, or using same-site cookies.

## GHSA-g2f5-gjr4-qjvm · gogs.io/gogs

2026-06-23 · Go · **HIGH** 8.7 · Pattern: `SSRF→INTERNAL_ACCESS`

### Root cause

The Gogs application allowed mirror repositories to follow HTTP redirects by default. An attacker could create a mirror with a public URL that, after a DNS change or a redirect, would point to an internal network resource. The application did not re-validate the mirror address against a local-network blocklist during subsequent sync operations, allowing access to internal services.

### Impact

An attacker could trick the Gogs server into making requests to internal network resources, potentially leading to information disclosure or unauthorized actions on internal services.

### Key diff

```
--- a/internal/database/mirror.go
+++ b/internal/database/mirror.go
@@ -216,15 +217,61 @@ func parseRemoteUpdateOutput(output string) []*mirrorSyncResult {
 	return results
 }
 
+// mirrorGitArgs returns the git-level arguments used by every remote network
+// operation against a mirror source.
+func mirrorGitArgs() []string {
+	// Disabling HTTP redirects prevents an attacker-controlled public URL from
+	// redirecting to an internal endpoint that the up-front clone address
+	// validation would otherwise have blocked.
+	return []string{"-c", "http.followRedirects=false"}
+}
+
 // runSync returns true if sync finished without error.
 func (m *Mirror) runSync() ([]*mirrorSyncResult, bool) {
 	repoPath := m.Repo.RepoPath()
 	wikiPath := m.Repo.WikiPath()
 	timeout := time.Duration(conf.Git.Timeout.Mirror) * time.Second
 
+	// Re-check the mirror address against the local-network blocklist on every
+	// sync. The address was validated when the mirror was created, but DNS for
+	// that hostname may have changed in the meantime to point at an internal
+	// host, so the up-front check is not sufficient on its own.
+	rawAddr := m.RawAddress()
+	if u, err := url.Parse(rawAddr); err == nil &&
+		(u.Scheme == "http" || u.Scheme == "https" || u.Scheme == "git") &&
+		netx.IsBlockedLocalHostname(u.Hostname(), conf.Security.LocalNetworkAllowlist) {
+		desc := fmt.Sprintf("Source URL of mirror repository '%s' resolves to a blocked local address: %s", m.Repo.FullName(), m.MosaicsAddress())
+		log.Error("Mirror.runSync: %s", desc)
+		if err := Handle.Notices().Create(context.TODO(), NoticeTypeRepository, desc); err != nil {
+			log.Error("CreateRepositoryNotice: %v", err)
+		}
+		return nil, false
+	}
+
 	// Do a fast-fail testing against on repository URL to ensure it is accessible under
 	// good condition to prevent long blocking on URL resolution without syncing anything.
-	if !git.IsURLAccessible(time.Minute, m.RawAddress()) {
+	if !isMirrorURLAccessible(time.Minute, rawAddr) {
 		desc := fmt.Sprintf("Source URL of mirror repository '%s' is not accessible: %s", m.Repo.FullName(), m.MosaicsAddress())
 		if err := Handle.Notices().Create(context.TODO(), NoticeTypeRepository, desc); err != nil {
 			log.Error("CreateRepositoryNotice: %v", err)
 		}
 		return nil, false
 	}
 
-	gitArgs := []string{"remote", "update"}
+	gitArgs := append(mirrorGitArgs(), "remote", "update")
```

### Fix summary

The patch disables HTTP redirects for all Git operations related to mirroring and migration by setting `http.followRedirects=false`. It also introduces a re-validation of mirror URLs against a local-network blocklist before each sync operation to prevent redirection to internal hosts.

## GHSA-pwpj-p52h-q484 · snipe/snipe-it

2026-06-23 · PHP · **HIGH** 8.5 · Pattern: `IDOR→DATA_ACCESS`

### Root cause

The application allowed users to specify a 'company_id' when creating or updating various assets (accessories, components, departments, consumables) via the API. Without proper validation, a malicious user could set this ID to a company they did not belong to, effectively injecting their data into another tenant's records.

### Impact

An attacker could create or modify assets within another company's account, leading to data pollution, unauthorized resource allocation, or potentially disrupting the target company's operations by manipulating their inventory or departmental structures.

### Key diff

```
--- a/app/Http/Controllers/Api/AccessoriesController.php
+++ b/app/Http/Controllers/Api/AccessoriesController.php
@@ -155,6 +156,7 @@ public function store(StoreAccessoryRequest $request)
     {
         $accessory = new Accessory;
         $accessory->fill($request->all());
+        $accessory->company_id = Company::getIdForCurrentUser($request->input('company_id'));
         $accessory = $request->handleImages($accessory);
 
         if ($accessory->save()) {
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a call to `Company::getIdForCurrentUser()` when setting the `company_id` for accessories, components, departments, and consumables. This ensures that the `company_id` is always validated against the current user's authorized companies, preventing cross-tenant data injection.

## GHSA-j3rv-43j4-c7qm · tools.jackson.core:jackson-databind

2026-06-23 · Java · **HIGH** 8.1 · Pattern: `DESERIALIZATION→OBJECT_INJECTION`

### Root cause

The `PolymorphicTypeValidator` in Jackson-databind, designed to restrict polymorphic deserialization to safe types, only validated the top-level container class. It failed to recursively validate generic type parameters or array component types, allowing an attacker to embed a gadget class within a seemingly safe container type (e.g., `ArrayList<EvilGadget>`).

### Impact

An attacker could bypass the `PolymorphicTypeValidator`'s security checks and achieve arbitrary class instantiation, potentially leading to remote code execution (RCE) if a suitable gadget class is available on the classpath.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/main/java/com/fasterxml/jackson/databind/DatabindContext.java
+++ b/src/main/java/com/fasterxml/jackson/databind/DatabindContext.java
@@ -283,9 +283,71 @@ private JavaType _resolveAndValidateGeneric(JavaType baseType, String subClass,
                 return _throwSubtypeClassNotAllowed(baseType, subClass, ptv);
             }
         }
+        for (int i = 0, n = subType.containedTypeCount(); i < n; ++i) {
+            _validateTypeParameter(baseType, subType.containedType(i), ptv, config);
+        }
+        if (subType.isArrayType()) {
+            _validateTypeParameter(baseType, subType.getContentType(), ptv, config);
+        }
         return subType;
     }
 
+    private void _validateTypeParameter(JavaType baseType, JavaType param,
+            PolymorphicTypeValidator ptv, MapperConfig<?> config)
+        throws JsonMappingException
+    {
+        final Class<?> raw = param.getRawClass();
+        if (raw != Object.class) {
+            final String rawName = raw.getName();
+            Validity vld = ptv.validateSubClassName(config, baseType, rawName);
+            if (vld == Validity.DENIED) {
+                throw invalidTypeIdException(baseType, rawName,
+                        "Configured `PolymorphicTypeValidator` (of type "
+                                + ClassUtil.classNameOf(ptv)
+                                + ") denied resolution of type parameter");
+            }
+            if (vld != Validity.ALLOWED) {
+                if (ptv.validateSubType(config, baseType, param) != Validity.ALLOWED) {
+                    throw invalidTypeIdException(baseType, rawName,
+                            "Configured `PolymorphicTypeValidator` (of type "
+                                    + ClassUtil.classNameOf(ptv)
+                                    + ") denied resolution of type parameter");
+                }
+            }
+        }
+        for (int i = 0, n = param.containedTypeCount(); i < n; ++i) {
+            _validateTypeParameter(baseType, param.containedType(i), ptv, config);
+        }
+        if (param.isArrayType()) {
+            _validateTypeParameter(baseType, param.getContentType(), ptv, config);
+        }
+    }
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a new recursive validation method `_validateTypeParameter` that is called for all generic type parameters and array component types. This ensures that every part of a deserialized type, including nested generics, is checked against the configured `PolymorphicTypeValidator` rules.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 3 occurrences**
> Languages: Java, PHP
> → GHSA-rmj7-2vxq-3g9f
> → GHSA-9369-69wj-7m2f

🔗 [View commit](https://github.com/FasterXML/jackson-databind/commit/434d6c511de7fdd9872f29157aafb6162d12d8d5)

## GHSA-rmj7-2vxq-3g9f · tools.jackson.core:jackson-databind

2026-06-23 · Java · **HIGH** 8.1 · Pattern: `DESERIALIZATION→OBJECT_INJECTION`

### Root cause

The `BasicPolymorphicTypeValidator` in Jackson-databind, when configured with `allowIfSubTypeIsArray()`, previously permitted any array type regardless of its element type. This meant that if a malicious class was denied by the sub-class allow-list, an attacker could wrap it in an array (e.g., `Evil[]`) to bypass the validation, as the array itself would be allowed, and the component would then be deserialized without further validation.

### Impact

An attacker could bypass the configured polymorphic type validation, potentially leading to the deserialization of arbitrary classes. This could result in remote code execution (RCE) if a gadget chain is available on the classpath, or other object injection attacks.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/main/java/com/fasterxml/jackson/databind/jsontype/BasicPolymorphicTypeValidator.java
+++ b/src/main/java/com/fasterxml/jackson/databind/jsontype/BasicPolymorphicTypeValidator.java
@@ -274,12 +296,8 @@ public Builder allowIfSubType(final TypeMatcher matcher) {
          * @since 2.11
          */
         public Builder allowIfSubTypeIsArray() {
-            return _appendSubClassMatcher(new TypeMatcher() {
-                @Override
-                public boolean match(MapperConfig<?> config, Class<?> clazz) {
-                    return clazz.isArray();
-                }
-            });
+            _acceptArrayTypes = true;
+            return this;
         }
 
         // 18-Nov-2019, tatu: alas, [databind#2539] can not be implemented with 2.x due
```

### Fix summary

The patch modifies the `allowIfSubTypeIsArray()` method in `BasicPolymorphicTypeValidator.Builder` to no longer simply allow all array types. Instead, it introduces an `_acceptArrayTypes` flag. When this flag is true, the validator now recursively unwraps array types and validates the innermost element type against the existing sub-class matchers, ensuring that array elements are also subject to the allow-list.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 3 occurrences**
> Languages: Java, PHP
> → GHSA-j3rv-43j4-c7qm
> → GHSA-9369-69wj-7m2f

## GHSA-wv27-2vqp-j7g5 · gogs.io/gogs

2026-06-23 · Go · **HIGH** 8.1 · Pattern: `SSRF→INTERNAL_ACCESS`

### Root cause

The application allowed users to specify a local file path as a mirror address for a repository without proper authorization checks. The `ParseRemoteAddr` function, which was responsible for validating and parsing remote addresses, did not consistently enforce the `CanImportLocal()` permission check for all call sites, specifically when setting a mirror address via the repository settings page. This allowed any authenticated user to import a local repository, effectively reading local files.

### Impact

An attacker could import local files from the server's filesystem into a Gogs repository, leading to information disclosure. This could potentially expose sensitive configuration files, user data, or other arbitrary files accessible by the Gogs process.

### Key diff

```
--- a/internal/route/repo/setting.go
+++ b/internal/route/repo/setting.go
@@ -121,7 +121,34 @@ func SettingsPost(c *context.Context, f form.RepoSetting) {
 				return
 			}
 		}
- 		if err := c.Repo.Mirror.SaveAddress(f.MirrorAddress); err != nil {
+ 		remoteAddr, err := form.ParseRemoteAddr(form.ParseRemoteAddrOptions{
+ 			CloneAddr: f.MirrorAddress,
+ 			User:      c.User,
+ 		})
+ 		if err != nil {
+ 			// ... error handling ...
+ 			return
+ 		}
+
+ 		if err := c.Repo.Mirror.SaveAddress(remoteAddr); err != nil {
```

### Fix summary

The patch refactors the `ParseRemoteAddr` function to accept an `options` struct, making the user and authentication details explicit. Crucially, it ensures that the `ParseRemoteAddr` function is called with the appropriate user context and its return value is used to validate and sanitize the mirror address before saving it, thereby enforcing the `CanImportLocal()` permission check for all relevant operations, including mirror settings.

## GHSA-6f75-x745-xcpr · snipe/snipe-it

2026-06-23 · PHP · **HIGH** 7.1 · Pattern: `PRIVILEGE_ESCALATION→ROLE`

### Root cause

The bulk user editing functionality in Snipe-IT allowed users with insufficient privileges to modify sensitive authentication-related fields such as `ldap_import` and `activated` status for other users. This was due to these fields being processed in a mass update query without proper per-user authorization checks for these specific fields.

### Impact

An attacker with bulk editing permissions could escalate their privileges or disable other users by changing their `activated` status or `ldap_import` setting, potentially affecting system integrity and user access control.

### Key diff

```
--- a/app/Http/Controllers/Users/BulkUsersController.php
+++ b/app/Http/Controllers/Users/BulkUsersController.php
@@ -171,8 +171,6 @@ public function update(Request $request)
             ->conditionallyAddItem('company_id')
             ->conditionallyAddItem('locale')
             ->conditionallyAddItem('remote')
--            ->conditionallyAddItem('ldap_import')
--            ->conditionallyAddItem('activated')
             ->conditionallyAddItem('display_name')
             ->conditionallyAddItem('start_date')
             ->conditionallyAddItem('end_date')
@@ -235,11 +233,21 @@ public function update(Request $request)
                 ->update(['location_id' => $this->update_array['location_id']]);
         }
 
-        // Only sync groups if groups were selected
-        if ($request->filled('groups')) {
-            foreach ($users as $user) {
-                if (auth()->user()->can('canEditAuthFields', $user) && auth()->user()->can('editableOnDemo')) {
+        // Fields that require canEditAuthFields (non-admins cannot touch admins/superusers,
+        // admins cannot touch superusers) must be applied per-user, not via mass update.
+        foreach ($users as $user) {
+            if (auth()->user()->can('canEditAuthFields', $user) && auth()->user()->can('editableOnDemo')) {
+                $authFieldUpdate = [];
+                if ($request->filled('activated')) {
+                    $authFieldUpdate['activated'] = $request->input('activated');
+                }
+                if ($request->filled('ldap_import')) {
+                    $authFieldUpdate['ldap_import'] = $request->input('ldap_import');
+                }
+                if (! empty($authFieldUpdate)) {
+                    $user->update($authFieldUpdate);
+                }
+                if ($request->filled('groups')) {
                     $user->groups()->sync($request->input('groups'));
                 }
             }
```

### Fix summary

The patch removes `ldap_import` and `activated` from the mass update query. Instead, these fields are now updated on a per-user basis, with explicit authorization checks (`canEditAuthFields`) applied to each user before modification, ensuring that only authorized users can alter these sensitive settings.

## GHSA-33g4-646g-qwmm · snipe/snipe-it

2026-06-23 · PHP · **MODERATE** 6.3 · Pattern: `MISSING_AUTHZ→RESOURCE`

### Root cause

The application allowed a user to update the 'company_id' of assets directly with an arbitrary ID provided in the request. This bypassed the multi-tenancy controls, as the system did not verify if the provided company ID belonged to the current user's authorized companies.

### Impact

An attacker could assign assets to companies they do not have legitimate access to, effectively bypassing multi-tenancy restrictions and potentially gaining unauthorized access to or control over assets belonging to other tenants.

### Key diff

```
-	$this->update_array['company_id'] = $request->input('company_id');
+	$this->update_array['company_id'] = Company::getIdForCurrentUser($request->input('company_id'));
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a call to `Company::getIdForCurrentUser()` when updating the `company_id`. This ensures that the provided company ID is validated against the companies the current user is authorized to manage, preventing unauthorized cross-tenant asset reassignment.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 69 occurrences**
> Languages: Go, Ruby, JavaScript, Python, PHP, Java, RUST, Erlang, C#

## GHSA-5hh8-q8hv-fr38 · tools.jackson.core:jackson-databind

2026-06-23 · Java · **MODERATE** 5.3 · Pattern: `MISSING_AUTHZ→RESOURCE`

### Root cause

The Jackson databind library failed to properly enforce `@JsonView` annotations for 'setterless' creator properties during deserialization. This meant that properties intended to be hidden or restricted by a view were still processed if they were part of a creator method and lacked a traditional setter.

### Impact

An attacker could bypass `@JsonView` restrictions, potentially populating properties that should not be accessible or modifiable under the active view, leading to unauthorized data manipulation or information disclosure.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/main/java/tools/jackson/databind/deser/bean/BeanDeserializer.java
+++ b/src/main/java/tools/jackson/databind/deser/bean/BeanDeserializer.java
@@ -728,6 +728,13 @@ protected Object _deserializeUsingPropertyBased(final JsonParser p, final Deseri
             int ix = _propNameMatcher.matchName(propName);
             if (ix >= 0) {
                 SettableBeanProperty prop = _propsByIndex[ix];
+                if ((activeView != null) && !prop.visibleInView(activeView)) {
+                    p.skipChildren();
+                    continue;
+                }
                 // [databind#3724]: Special handling because Records' ignored creator props
                 // weren't removed (to help in creating constructor-backed PropertyCreator)
                 // so they ended up in _beanProperties, unlike POJO (whose ignored
```

### Fix summary

The patch adds a check within the `_deserializeUsingPropertyBased` method to explicitly verify if a property is visible in the active `JsonView`. If the property is not visible, the parser now skips its children, preventing its deserialization.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 69 occurrences**
> Languages: Go, Ruby, JavaScript, Python, PHP, Java, RUST, Erlang, C#

## GHSA-3wrr-7qpf-2prh · com.fasterxml.jackson.core:jackson-databind

2026-06-23 · Java · **MODERATE** 0.0 · Pattern: `DOS→RESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The `toString()` method for deeply nested `JsonNode` structures in Jackson-databind used a recursive approach. When processing a `JsonNode` with a very large depth, each recursive call consumed stack memory, eventually leading to a `StackOverflowError` and crashing the application.

### Impact

An attacker could provide a specially crafted, deeply nested JSON input to an application that processes it using Jackson-databind's `toString()` method, causing the application to crash due to a `StackOverflowError`, leading to a denial of service.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/main/java/com/fasterxml/jackson/databind/node/InternalNodeMapper.java
+++ b/src/main/java/com/fasterxml/jackson/databind/node/InternalNodeMapper.java
@@ -92,31 +94,100 @@ public void serializeWithType(JsonGenerator g, SerializerProvider ctxt, TypeSeri
             serialize(g, ctxt);
         }
 
-    
         protected void _serializeNonRecursive(JsonGenerator g, JsonNode node) throws IOException
         {
             if (node instanceof ObjectNode) {
-                g.writeStartObject(this);
-                Iterator<Map.Entry<String, JsonNode>> it = node.fields();
-                while (it.hasNext()) {
-                    Map.Entry<String, JsonNode> en = it.next();
-                    JsonNode value = en.getValue();
-                    g.writeFieldName(en.getKey());
-                    value.serialize(g, _context);
-                }
-                g.writeEndObject();
+                g.writeStartObject(this, node.size());
+                _serializeNonRecursive(g, new IteratorStack(), node.fields());
             } else if (node instanceof ArrayNode) {
                 g.writeStartArray(this, node.size());
-                Iterator<JsonNode> it = node.elements();
-                while (it.hasNext()) {
-                    // For now, assuming it's either BaseJsonNode, JsonSerializable
-                    JsonNode value = it.next();
-                    value.serialize(g, _context);
-                }
```

### Fix summary

The patch refactors the `_serializeNonRecursive` method to use an explicit `IteratorStack` instead of relying on Java's call stack for traversing nested `JsonNode` structures. This iterative approach prevents `StackOverflowError` for deeply nested JSON by managing the traversal state on the heap rather than the stack.

## GHSA-f3c5-6cw8-fg57 · snipe/snipe-it

2026-06-23 · PHP · **MODERATE** 0.0 · Pattern: `MISSING_AUTHZ→RESOURCE`

### Root cause

Several API selectlist endpoints in Snipe-IT, specifically for Accessories, Users, Assets, and Consumables, lacked proper authorization checks. This allowed any authenticated user to access these selectlists, regardless of whether they had the necessary permissions to view the underlying data.

### Impact

An attacker could potentially enumerate or gain unauthorized access to sensitive information such as accessory details, user lists, asset information, and consumable data, even if their role should not permit such access.

### Key diff

```
--- a/app/Http/Controllers/Api/AccessoriesController.php
+++ b/app/Http/Controllers/Api/AccessoriesController.php
@@ -401,6 +401,7 @@ public function checkin(Request $request, $accessoryUserId = null)
      */
     public function selectlist(Request $request)
     {
+        $this->authorize('view.selectlists');
 
         $accessories = Accessory::select([
             'accessories.id',
```

### Fix summary

The patch adds a call to `$this->authorize('view.selectlists');` at the beginning of the `selectlist` method in the `Api/AccessoriesController.php`, `Api/UsersController.php`, `Api/AssetsController.php`, and `Api/ConsumablesController.php` files. This ensures that only users with the `view.selectlists` permission can access these API endpoints.

## GHSA-hf68-g98v-wp9g · snipe/snipe-it

2026-06-23 · PHP · **MODERATE** 0.0 · Pattern: `PRIVILEGE_ESCALATION→ROLE`

### Root cause

The application allowed users with 'canEditAuthFields' permission to modify user groups during user creation. This permission was not sufficiently restricted to only superusers, enabling an attacker with this specific permission to elevate their privileges by assigning themselves or other users to administrative groups.

### Impact

An attacker could escalate their privileges to that of an administrator by assigning themselves to an administrative group, gaining full control over the application.

### Key diff

```
--- a/app/Http/Controllers/Users/UsersController.php
+++ b/app/Http/Controllers/Users/UsersController.php
@@ -164,7 +164,7 @@ public function store(SaveUserRequest $request)
 
             }
 
-            if (auth()->user()->can('canEditAuthFields', $user) && auth()->user()->can('editableOnDemo')) {
+            if (auth()->user()->isSuperUser() && auth()->user()->can('editableOnDemo')) {
                 $user->groups()->sync($request->input('groups'));
             }
```

### Fix summary

The patch changes the permission check from `auth()->user()->can('canEditAuthFields', $user)` to `auth()->user()->isSuperUser()`. This ensures that only superusers can modify user groups during user creation, preventing unauthorized privilege escalation.

## GHSA-r6fj-869h-4f6q · io.netty.incubator:netty-incubator-codec-ohttp

2026-06-23 · Java · **MODERATE** 0.0 · Pattern: `UNCLASSIFIED`

### Root cause

The OHttpVersionChunkDraft decoder did not enforce the presence of a final chunk when the complete body was expected. This allowed an attacker to prematurely terminate an OHTTP stream without the server detecting the truncation, leading to an incomplete or malformed message being processed.

### Impact

An attacker could send truncated OHTTP messages, potentially bypassing security checks, causing application errors, or leading to unexpected behavior due to incomplete data processing.

### Key diff

```
--- a/codec-ohttp/src/main/java/io/netty/incubator/codec/ohttp/OHttpVersionChunkDraft.java
+++ b/codec-ohttp/src/main/java/io/netty/incubator/codec/ohttp/OHttpVersionChunkDraft.java
@@ -172,13 +172,18 @@ public void parse(ByteBufAllocator alloc, ByteBuf in, boolean completeBodyReceiv
                 return;
             }
         }
+        boolean finalChunk = false;
         while (in.isReadable()) {
             ChunkInfo chunkInfo = parseNextChunk(in, completeBodyReceived, maxChunkSize);
             if (chunkInfo == null) {
                 break;
             }
+            finalChunk |= chunkInfo.isFinal;
             decoder.decodeChunk(alloc, in, chunkInfo.length, chunkInfo.isFinal, out);
         }
+        if (completeBodyReceived && !finalChunk) {
+            throw new CorruptedFrameException("OHTTP stream ended without a final chunk");
+        }
     }
 
     @Override
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a boolean flag `finalChunk` to track if a final chunk has been received. After processing all available chunks, if `completeBodyReceived` is true but `finalChunk` is false, a `CorruptedFrameException` is thrown, ensuring that truncated streams are detected.

## GHSA-vcm5-gvmp-78mp · gogs.io/gogs

2026-06-23 · Go · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→XSS`

### Root cause

The application was displaying user-controlled milestone names directly into the HTML without proper sanitization. This allowed an attacker to inject malicious scripts by crafting a milestone name containing JavaScript.

### Impact

An attacker could execute arbitrary JavaScript in the victim's browser, leading to session hijacking, defacement, or redirection to malicious sites.

### Key diff

```
- <div class="item" data-id="{{.ID}}" data-href="{{$.RepoLink}}/issues?milestone={{.ID}}"> {{.Name}}</div>
+ <div class="item" data-id="{{.ID}}" data-href="{{$.RepoLink}}/issues?milestone={{.ID}}"> {{.Name | Sanitize}}</div>
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces the `| Sanitize` template function to the display of milestone names. This ensures that any HTML or script tags within the milestone name are properly escaped before being rendered in the browser, preventing XSS.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 71 occurrences**
> Languages: Python, JavaScript, PHP, Java, Go, RUST, Ruby
